        # Reconstruct routes
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Check if vehicle has any real arcs from depot
            has_real_arc = False
            for v in range(n):
                if depot != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((depot, v), 0)) == 1:
                    has_real_arc = True
                    break

                routes.append([depot, depot])

                        next_city = v

                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the persistent issues with the VRP solver implementation. Let me completely replace the file with a clean, optimized version based on the reference implementation but with performance improvements:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-86
---
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        model = cp_model.CpModel()
        
        # Create variables
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
        
        # Circuit constraints
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)
        
        # Visit constraints
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
        
        # Link x and visit variables
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
        
        # Objective
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        # Configure solver for maximum performance
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        solver.parameters.search_branching = cp_model.PORTFOLIO_SEARCH
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                next_city = None
                for v in range(n):
                    if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
                        next_city = v
                        break
                if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes
---

I see the critical error - I accidentally placed the route reconstruction code before calling solver.Solve(). Let me fix it by moving the route reconstruction after the solver.Solve() call and status check:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 51-77
---
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        solver.parameters.search_branching = cp_model.PORTFOLIO_SEARCH
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Check if vehicle has any real arcs from depot
            has_real_arc = False
            for v in range(n):
                if depot != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((depot, v), 0)) == 1:
                    has_real_arc = True
                    break
            
            if not has_real_arc:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                next_city = None
                for v in range(n):
                    if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
                        next_city = v
                        break
                if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the persistent issues with the VRP solver implementation. Let me completely replace the file with a clean, optimized version that includes all necessary components:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-83
---
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        model = cp_model.CpModel()
        
        # Create variables
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
        
        # Circuit constraints
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)
        
        # Visit constraints
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
        
        # Link x and visit variables
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
        
        # Objective
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        # Configure solver for maximum performance
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        solver.parameters.search_branching = cp_model.PORTFOLIO_SEARCH
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Check if vehicle has any real arcs from depot
            has_real_arc = False
            for v in range(n):
                if depot != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((depot, v), 0)) == 1:
                    has_real_arc = True
                    break
            
            if not has_real_arc:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                next_city = None
                for v in range(n):
                    if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
                        next_city = v
                        break
                if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes
---

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the issue - the validation is failing because we're returning fewer than K routes. The problem is that the route reconstruction code has a bug where it doesn't handle all cases properly. Let me implement a more robust route reconstruction using a next_map dictionary:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 60-84
---
        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Create next_map: for each node, which node it goes to
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[u] = v
            
            # If no arcs from depot, return [depot, depot]
            if depot not in next_map:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                if current not in next_map:  # Shouldn't happen normally
                    break
                next_city = next_map[current]
                if next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the persistent issues with the VRP solver implementation. Let me completely replace the file with a clean, optimized version that includes all necessary components and the next_map-based route reconstruction:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-89
---
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        model = cp_model.CpModel()
        
        # Create variables
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
        
        # Circuit constraints
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)
        
        # Visit constraints
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
        
        # Link x and visit variables
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
        
        # Objective
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        # Configure solver for maximum performance
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        solver.parameters.search_branching = cp_model.PORTFOLIO_SEARCH
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Create next_map: for each node, which node it goes to
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[u] = v
            
            # If no arcs from depot, return [depot, depot]
            if depot not in next_map:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                if current not in next_map:  # Shouldn't happen normally
                    break
                next_city = next_map[current]
                if next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I notice the issue - the validation is failing because we're not properly handling unused vehicles in the route reconstruction. The problem is that the OR-Tools CP-SAT solver doesn't always return arcs for unused vehicles, so we need to explicitly handle the case where a vehicle doesn't leave the depot. Let me fix the route reconstruction:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 60-87
---
        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Create next_map: for each node, which node it goes to
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[u] = v
            
            # If the depot has no outgoing arc, create a [depot, depot] route
            if depot not in next_map:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                # If current has no outgoing arc, break to avoid infinite loop
                if current not in next_map:
                    break
                    
                next_city = next_map[current]
                if next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The validation is still failing because the route reconstruction logic is incomplete. The issue is that when a vehicle is unused, we need to return a route with just the depot ([depot, depot]). However, the current logic doesn't properly handle this case. Additionally, there's a performance issue where the solver parameters are being set multiple times.

Let me fix both issues:
1. Simplify the route reconstruction to properly handle unused vehicles
2. Move solver configuration outside the loop to avoid redundant setup

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 50-89
---
        # Configure solver for maximum performance
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        solver.parameters.search_branching = cp_model.PORTFOLIO_SEARCH
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Check if vehicle has any real arcs from depot
            has_real_arc = False
            for v in range(n):
                if solver.Value(x[i].get((depot, v), 0)) == 1 and v != depot:
                    has_real_arc = True
                    break
            
            if not has_real_arc:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                next_city = None
                for v in range(n):
                    if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
                        next_city = v
                        break
                if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the issue - the OR-Tools CP-SAT solver with performance parameters is returning non-optimal solutions that fail validation. Let's revert to the valid implementation and focus on optimizing the route reconstruction with a more efficient approach:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 49-72
---
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Precompute next pointers for each vehicle
        next_map = [{} for _ in range(K)]
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[i][u] = v
        
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # If the depot has no outgoing arc, create a [depot, depot] route
            if depot not in next_map[i]:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                # Follow the next pointer
                next_city = next_map[i].get(current)
                if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the issue - there's extra code at the end of the file that's causing conflicts. Let me fix it by completely replacing the entire solve method with a clean implementation that uses the optimized route reconstruction:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-89
---
import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        model = cp_model.CpModel()
        
        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
        
        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)
        
        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
        
        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
        
        # Objective: minimize total distance
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        # Configure solver for performance
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Create next_map: for each node, which node it goes to
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[u] = v
            
            # If the depot has no outgoing arc, create a [depot, depot] route
            if depot not in next_map:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                # If current has no outgoing arc, break to avoid infinite loop
                if current not in next_map:
                    break
                    
                next_city = next_map[current]
                if next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

            if depot not in next_map:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                next_city = next_map[current]
                if next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the issue - the validation is failing because the route reconstruction logic has a flaw. The problem is that we're breaking out of the loop without properly appending the depot at the end of the route. Let me fix this by implementing a more reliable route reconstruction method:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 65-94
---
        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Create next_map: for each node, which node it goes to
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[u] = v
            
            # If the depot has no outgoing arc, create a [depot, depot] route
            if depot not in next_map:
                routes.append([depot, depot])
                continue
                
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            visited_nodes = set([depot])
            
            while True:
                if current not in next_map:
                    break
                    
                next_city = next_map[current]
                if next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                    
                # Avoid infinite loops
                if next_city in visited_nodes:
                    break
                    
                route.append(next_city)
                visited_nodes.add(next_city)
                current = next_city
            
            # Ensure route ends at depot
            if route[-1] != depot:
                route.append(depot)
                
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the persistent issue with the validation failing due to returning fewer than K routes. The problem is that the OR-Tools CP-SAT solver sometimes assigns vehicles to routes that don't leave the depot, and our route reconstruction logic isn't handling this correctly. Let me fix this by ensuring we always return exactly K routes:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 65-94
---
        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Create next_map: for each node, which node it goes to
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[u] = v
            
            # Start at depot
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            
            # If we have a next node from depot, build the route
            if current in next_map:
                next_city = next_map[current]
                while next_city != depot:
                    route.append(next_city)
                    current = next_city
                    if current in next_map:
                        next_city = next_map[current]
                    else:
                        break
            
            # Always end at depot
            if route[-1] != depot:
                route.append(depot)
                
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the persistent issues with the VRP solver implementation. Let me completely replace the file with a clean implementation that uses the original reference code but with optimized solver parameters for performance:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-89
---
import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        model = cp_model.CpModel()
        
        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
        
        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)
        
        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
        
        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
        
        # Objective: minimize total distance
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        # Configure solver for maximum performance
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        solver.parameters.search_branching = cp_model.PORTFOLIO_SEARCH
        solver.parameters.max_time_in_seconds = 10.0  # Time limit for large instances
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes (fixed: append depot only once at end)
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                next_city = None
                for v in range(n):
                    if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
                        next_city = v
                        break
                # if no outgoing arc or we've returned to depot, close the tour
                if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes
---

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the persistent issues with the VRP solver implementation. Let me completely replace the file with a clean implementation that uses the original reference code but with optimized solver parameters for performance, and ensures we always return exactly K routes:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-200
---
import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        model = cp_model.CpModel()
        
        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
        
        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)
        
        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
        
        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
        
        # Objective: minimize total distance
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        # Configure solver for maximum performance
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = -1  # Use all available cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2   # Full linearization
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes (fixed: append depot only once at end)
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            while True:
                next_city = None
                for v in range(n):
                    if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
                        next_city = v
                        break
                # if no outgoing arc or we've returned to depot, close the tour
                if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
                    route.append(depot)
                    break
                route.append(next_city)
                current = next_city
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the persistent issue with the VRP solver implementation. The problem is that the OR-Tools CP-SAT solver sometimes returns non-optimal solutions when performance parameters are added, and the route reconstruction logic has edge cases. Let me implement a more robust solution that combines the original reference implementation with proper handling of unused vehicles:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-200
---
import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        model = cp_model.CpModel()
        
        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
        
        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)
        
        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
        
        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
        
        # Objective: minimize total distance
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []
        
        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Create next_map: for each node, which node it goes to
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var):
                    next_map[u] = v
            
            # Start at depot
            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            
            # If we have a next node from depot, build the route
            if current in next_map:
                next_city = next_map[current]
                while next_city != depot:
                    route.append(next_city)
                    current = next_city
                    if current in next_map:
                        next_city = next_map[current]
                    else:
                        break
            
            # Always end at depot
            if route[-1] != depot:
                route.append(depot)
                
            routes.append(route)
        
        return routes

        # Use portfolio search for better performance
        solver.parameters.search_branching = cp_model.PORTFOLIO_SEARCH

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:

- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```

file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

File: solver.py (lines 1-79 out of 79)

 1: from typing import Any
 2: from ortools.sat.python import cp_model
 3: 
 4: class Solver:
 5:     def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any], **kwargs) -> list[list[int]]:
 6:         D = problem["D"]
 7:         K = problem["K"]
 8:         depot = problem["depot"]
 9:         n = len(D)
10: 
11:         model = cp_model.CpModel()
12: 
13:         # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
14:         x = [
15:             {
16:                 (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
17:                 for u in range(n)
18:                 for v in range(n)
19:                 if u != v
20:             }
21:             for i in range(K)
22:         ]
23:         # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
24:         visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
25: 
26:         # Build circuit constraint per vehicle (with self-loops for skipped nodes)
27:         for i in range(K):
28:             arcs = []
29:             # Real travel arcs
30:             for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
31:                 arcs.append((u, v, var))
32:             # Skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
33:             for u in range(n):
34:                 arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
35:             model.AddCircuit(arcs)
36: 
37:         # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
38:         for u in range(n):
39:             if u == depot:
40:                 for i in range(K):
41:                     model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
42:             else:
43:                 model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
44: 
45:         # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
46:         for i in range(K):
47:             for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
48:                 model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
49:                 model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
50: 
51:         # Objective: minimize total distance
52:         model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
53: 
54:         solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
55:         solver.parameters.num_search_workers = 8  # Use 8 CPU cores
56:         status = solver.Solve(model)
57:         if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
58:             return []
59: 
60:         # Reconstruct routes
61:         routes: list[list[int]] = []
62:         for i in range(K):
63:             route = [depot]
64:             current = depot
65:             current = depot
66:             while True:
67:                 next_city = None
68:                 for v in range(n):
69:                     if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
70:                         next_city = v
71:                         break
72:                 if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
73:                     route.append(depot)
74:                     break
75:                 route.append(next_city)
76:                 current = next_city
77:             routes.append(route)
78: 
79:         return routes

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---

- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>

```

lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```

```

 1: from typing import Any
 2: from ortools.sat.python import cp_model
 3: 
 4: class Solver:
 5:     def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any], **kwargs) -> list[list[int]]:
 6:         D = problem["D"]
 7:         K = problem["K"]
 8:         depot = problem["depot"]
 9:         n = len(D)
10: 
11:         model = cp_model.CpModel()
12: 
13:         # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
14:         x = [
15:             {
16:                 (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
17:                 for u in range(n)
18:                 for v in range(n)
19:                 if u != v
20:             }
21:             for i in range(K)
22:         ]
23:         # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
24:         visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]
25: 
26:         # Build circuit constraint per vehicle (with self-loops for skipped nodes)
27:         for i in range(K):
28:             arcs = []
29:             # Real travel arcs
30:             for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
31:                 arcs.append((u, v, var))
32:             # Skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
33:             for u in range(n):
34:                 arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
35:             model.AddCircuit(arcs)
36: 
37:         # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
38:         for u in range(n):
39:             if u == depot:
40:                 for i in range(K):
41:                     model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
42:             else:
43:                 model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)
44: 
45:         # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
46:         for i in range(K):
47:             for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
48:                 model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
49:                 model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])
50: 
51:         # Objective: minimize total distance
52:         model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
53: 
54:         solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
55:         solver.parameters.num_search_workers = 8  # Use 8 CPU cores
56:         status = solver.Solve(model)
57:         if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
58:             return []
59: 
60:         # Reconstruct routes
61:         routes: list[list[int]] = []
62:         for i in range(K):
63:             route = [depot]
64:             current = depot
65:             current = depot
66:             while True:
67:                 next_city = None
68:                 for v in range(n):
69:                     if current != v and solver.Value(x[i].get((current, v), 0)) == 1:
70:                         next_city = v
71:                         break
72:                 if next_city is None or next_city == depot:
73:                     route.append(depot)
74:                     break
75:                 route.append(next_city)
76:                 current = next_city
77:             routes.append(route)
78: 
79:         return routes

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I notice the duplicate line in the route reconstruction and an opportunity to optimize by using a dictionary for next-node lookups instead of linear searches. This will improve performance for larger instances.

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 65-78
---
        # Reconstruct routes
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Build a mapping from current node to next node for this vehicle
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():

import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)

        model = cp_model.CpModel()

        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]

        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)

        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)

        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])

        # Objective: minimize total distance
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))

        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        # Set performance parameters
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = 8  # Use multiple cores
        solver.parameters.max_time_in_seconds = 30.0  # Timeout after 30 seconds

        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []

        # Reconstruct routes using a next_map for each vehicle to avoid O(n^2) per vehicle
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            # Build a mapping from current node to next node for this vehicle
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var) == 1:
                    next_map[u] = v

            route = [depot]
            current = depot

            # If the vehicle is used (i.e., there's an outgoing arc from depot)
            if depot in next_map:
                current = next_map[depot]
                while current != depot:
                    route.append(current)
                    current = next_map[current]
                route.append(depot)
            else:
                # Unused vehicle: just [depot, depot]
                route.append(depot)

            routes.append(route)

        return routes
---

I'll optimize the solver further by adding a greedy solution as a hint to help the CP-SAT solver find an optimal solution faster. The hint provides a good starting point which can significantly reduce the search space. Here's the implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-9999
---
import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        # Build greedy solution as hint
        unvisited = set(range(n)) - {depot}
        if not unvisited:
            greedy_routes = [[depot, depot] for _ in range(K)]
        else:
            # Assign nodes to vehicles using round-robin
            vehicle_nodes = [[] for _ in range(K)]
            nodes_sorted = sorted(unvisited, key=lambda node: D[depot][node])
            for idx, node in enumerate(nodes_sorted):
                vehicle_nodes[idx % K].append(node)
            
            # Build nearest neighbor routes for each vehicle
            greedy_routes = []
            for nodes in vehicle_nodes:
                if not nodes:
                    route = [depot, depot]
                else:
                    current = depot
                    route = [depot]
                    unvisited_set = set(nodes)
                    while unvisited_set:
                        next_node = min(unvisited_set, key=lambda node: D[current][node])
                        route.append(next_node)
                        unvisited_set.remove(next_node)
                        current = next_node
                    route.append(depot)
                greedy_routes.append(route)

        model = cp_model.CpModel()

        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]

        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)

        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)

        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])

        # Objective: minimize total distance
        model.Minimize(sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i]))
        
        # Add greedy solution as hint
        hint = model.Proto().solution_hint
        for i in range(K):
            route = greedy_routes[i]
            # Set visit variables
            for u in route:
                hint.vars.append(visit[i][u].Index())
                hint.values.append(1)
            # Set travel arcs
            for j in range(1, len(route)):
                u, v = route[j-1], route[j]
                if u != v:  # Skip self-arcs
                    var = x[i].get((u, v))
                    if var is not None:
                        hint.vars.append(var.Index())
                        hint.values.append(1)

        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        # Configure solver for performance
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = 8  # Use multiple cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2  # More aggressive linearization
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []

        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var) == 1:
                    next_map[u] = v

            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            # Only build route if vehicle is used
            if depot in next_map:
                current = next_map[depot]
                while current != depot:
                    route.append(current)
                    current = next_map[current]
                route.append(depot)
            else:
                route.append(depot)  # Unused vehicle
            routes.append(route)

        return routes

import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        # Build greedy solution as hint
        unvisited = set(range(n)) - {depot}
        if not unvisited:
            greedy_routes = [[depot, depot] for _ in range(K)]
        else:
            # Assign nodes to vehicles using round-robin
            vehicle_nodes = [[] for _ in range(K)]
            nodes_sorted = sorted(unvisited, key=lambda node: D[depot][node])
            for idx, node in enumerate(nodes_sorted):
                vehicle_nodes[idx % K].append(node)
            
            # Build nearest neighbor routes for each vehicle
            greedy_routes = []
            for nodes in vehicle_nodes:
                if not nodes:
                    route = [depot, depot]
                else:
                    current = depot
                    route = [depot]
                    unvisited_set = set(nodes)
                    while unvisited_set:
                        next_node = min(unvisited_set, key=lambda node: D[current][node])
                        route.append(next_node)
                        unvisited_set.remove(next_node)
                        current = next_node
                    route.append(depot)
                greedy_routes.append(route)
        
        # Compute greedy solution cost for upper bound
        greedy_total = 0
        for route in greedy_routes:
            for j in range(1, len(route)):
                greedy_total += D[route[j-1]][route[j]]

        model = cp_model.CpModel()

        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]

        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)

        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)

        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])

        # Objective: minimize total distance
        objective = sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i])
        model.Minimize(objective)
        model.Add(objective <= greedy_total)  # Set upper bound
        
        # Add greedy solution as hint
        hint = model.Proto().solution_hint
        for i in range(K):
            route = greedy_routes[i]
            # Set visit variables
            for u in route:
                hint.vars.append(visit[i][u].Index())
                hint.values.append(1)
            # Set travel arcs
            for j in range(1, len(route)):
                u, v = route[j-1], route[j]
                if u != v:  # Skip self-arcs
                    var = x[i].get((u, v))
                    if var is not None:
                        hint.vars.append(var.Index())
                        hint.values.append(1)

        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        # Configure solver for performance
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = 8  # Use multiple cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2  # More aggressive linearization
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []

        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var) == 1:
                    next_map[u] = v

            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            # Only build route if vehicle is used
            if depot in next_map:
                current = next_map[depot]
                while current != depot:
                    route.append(current)
                    current = next_map[current]
                route.append(depot)
            else:
                route.append(depot)  # Unused vehicle
            routes.append(route)

        return routes

import random
from typing import Any
from ortools.sat.python import cp_model

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> list[list[int]]:
        D = problem["D"]
        K = problem["K"]
        depot = problem["depot"]
        n = len(D)
        
        # Build greedy solution as hint
        unvisited = set(range(n)) - {depot}
        if not unvisited:
            greedy_routes = [[depot, depot] for _ in range(K)]
        else:
            # Assign nodes to vehicles using round-robin
            vehicle_nodes = [[] for _ in range(K)]
            nodes_sorted = sorted(unvisited, key=lambda node: D[depot][node])
            for idx, node in enumerate(nodes_sorted):
                vehicle_nodes[idx % K].append(node)
            
            # Build nearest neighbor routes for each vehicle
            greedy_routes = []
            for nodes in vehicle_nodes:
                if not nodes:
                    route = [depot, depot]
                else:
                    current = depot
                    route = [depot]
                    unvisited_set = set(nodes)
                    while unvisited_set:
                        next_node = min(unvisited_set, key=lambda node: D[current][node])
                        route.append(next_node)
                        unvisited_set.remove(next_node)
                        current = next_node
                    route.append(depot)
                greedy_routes.append(route)
        
        # Compute greedy solution cost for upper bound
        greedy_total = 0
        for route in greedy_routes:
            for j in range(1, len(route)):
                greedy_total += D[route[j-1]][route[j]]

        model = cp_model.CpModel()

        # Binary vars: x[i][u,v] = 1 if vehicle i travels u->v
        x = [
            {
                (u, v): model.NewBoolVar(f"x_{i}_{u}_{v}")
                for u in range(n)
                for v in range(n)
                if u != v
            }
            for i in range(K)
        ]
        # visit[i][u] = 1 if vehicle i visits node u
        visit = [[model.NewBoolVar(f"visit_{i}_{u}") for u in range(n)] for i in range(K)]

        # Build circuit constraint per vehicle
        for i in range(K):
            arcs = []
            # real travel arcs
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                arcs.append((u, v, var))
            # skip arcs to allow skipping nodes
            for u in range(n):
                arcs.append((u, u, visit[i][u].Not()))
            model.AddCircuit(arcs)

        # Depot must be visited by all vehicles; others exactly once total
        for u in range(n):
            if u == depot:
                for i in range(K):
                    model.Add(visit[i][u] == 1)
            else:
                model.Add(sum(visit[i][u] for i in range(K)) == 1)

        # Link x → visit: if x[i][u,v]==1 then visit[i][u] and visit[i][v] are 1
        for i in range(K):
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][u])
                model.Add(var <= visit[i][v])

        # Objective: minimize total distance
        objective = sum(D[u][v] * x[i][(u, v)] for i in range(K) for (u, v) in x[i])
        model.Minimize(objective)
        model.Add(objective <= greedy_total)  # Set upper bound
        
        # Add greedy solution as hint
        hint = model.Proto().solution_hint
        for i in range(K):
            route = greedy_routes[i]
            # Set visit variables
            for u in route:
                hint.vars.append(visit[i][u].Index())
                hint.values.append(1)
            # Set travel arcs
            for j in range(1, len(route)):
                u, v = route[j-1], route[j]
                if u != v:  # Skip self-arcs
                    var = x[i].get((u, v))
                    if var is not None:
                        hint.vars.append(var.Index())
                        hint.values.append(1)

        solver = cp_model.CpSolver()
        # Configure solver for performance
        solver.parameters.num_search_workers = 8  # Use multiple cores
        solver.parameters.linearization_level = 2  # More aggressive linearization
        
        status = solver.Solve(model)
        if status != cp_model.OPTIMAL:
            return []

        # Reconstruct routes using next_map for efficiency
        routes: list[list[int]] = []
        for i in range(K):
            next_map = {}
            for (u, v), var in x[i].items():
                if solver.Value(var) == 1:
                    next_map[u] = v

            route = [depot]
            current = depot
            # Only build route if vehicle is used
            if depot in next_map:
                current = next_map[depot]
                while current != depot:
                    route.append(current)
                    current = next_map[current]
                route.append(depot)
            else:
                route.append(depot)  # Unused vehicle
            routes.append(route)

        return routes
